Full text of "Nottinghamshire parish registers"

See other formats 


This is a digital copy of a book that was preserved for generations on library shelves before it was carefully scanned by Google as part of a project 
to make the world's books discoverable online. 

It has survived long enough for the copyright to expire and the book to enter the public domain. A public domain book is one that was never subject 
to copyright or whose legal copyright term has expired. Whether a book is in the public domain may vary country to country. Public domain books 
are our gateways to the past, representing a wealth of history, culture and knowledge that's often difficult to discover. 

Marks, notations and other marginalia present in the original volume will appear in this file - a reminder of this book's long journey from the 
publisher to a library and finally to you. 

Usage guidelines 

Google is proud to partner with libraries to digitize public domain materials and make them widely accessible. Public domain books belong to the 
public and we are merely their custodians. Nevertheless, this work is expensive, so in order to keep providing this resource, we have taken steps to 
prevent abuse by commercial parties, including placing technical restrictions on automated querying. 

We also ask that you: 

+ Make non-commercial use of the files We designed Google Book Search for use by individuals, and we request that you use these files for 
personal, non-commercial purposes. 

+ Refrain from automated querying Do not send automated queries of any sort to Google's system: If you are conducting research on machine 
translation, optical character recognition or other areas where access to a large amount of text is helpful, please contact us. We encourage the 
use of public domain materials for these purposes and may be able to help. 

+ Maintain attribution The Google "watermark" you see on each file is essential for informing people about this project and helping them find 
additional materials through Google Book Search. Please do not remove it. 

+ Keep it legal Whatever your use, remember that you are responsible for ensuring that what you are doing is legal. Do not assume that just 
because we believe a book is in the public domain for users in the United States, that the work is also in the public domain for users in other 
countries. Whether a book is still in copyright varies from country to country, and we can't offer guidance on whether any specific use of 
any specific book is allowed. Please do not assume that a book's appearance in Google Book Search means it can be used in any manner 
anywhere in the world. Copyright infringement liability can be quite severe. 

About Google Book Search 

Google's mission is to organize the world's information and to make it universally accessible and useful. Google Book Search helps readers 
discover the world's books while helping authors and publishers reach new audiences. You can search through the full text of this book on the web

PREFACE. 



The present is the ninth volume of Nottingham shhre Pari^ 
Registers, and includes marriage registers in the south part 
of Broxtowe Wapentake. Two parishes, Bunny and Langar, 
in the Wapentakes of Bingham and Rushcliffe respectively, 
are also included. It was found impassible to obtain the 
transcript of these registers in time for inclusion in their 
appropriate volumes. The number of registers is less than in 
former volumes, but the population of several of the villages 
included is much greater than the average of the parishes 
whose registers have already been printed. Thanks are due 
to the parish clergy who have permitted their registers to be 
printed. Those in the present volume have been transcribed 
by Mr. T. M. Blagg, Mr. F. A. Wadsworth, Rev. H Cooper, 
Rev. J. E. Phillips and Mr. A. Stapleton. 

The entries, as before, have been reduced to a common 
form, and the following abbreviations adopted : ‚Äî 

w.=widower or widow. p.^^of the parish of. 

s.¬ª8pinster, single woman, co.¬ªin the county of. 

or son. dioc">in the diocese of. 

b.¬ªbachelor or single man. /ic^marriage licence. 

d.s¬ªdaughter of. f.w.k.== frame- work-knitter. 

The spelling of the surnames is in all cases the same as in 
the original registers, but the Christian names have in most 
cases been translated or modernised. 

It must be remembered that these printed abstracts of 
marriage registers are not ** evidence** in the technical sense. 
Certified copies must still be obtained when evidence of a 
marriage is needed for proving a pedigree in a court of law, 
or when registering it at Heralds* College. For such certifi- 
cates application must be made to the clergy in charge of the 
original registers. 

It should be borne in mind that previous to 1752 the years 
were calculated as b^^ning on the a5th of March, so that a 



VI 

marriage entered as having taken place on, say, the 20th of 
February, 1624, really occurred on that day in 1625 according 
to our reckoning. This is sometimes expressed by "162J" or 
1624-5 

No index is issued with the volume, as the Editors believe 
that it is better to print as many registers as possible, and to 
defer index- making until the registers still in manuscript are 
placed beyond the risk of loss. 

Volume X is already in the printer's hands and will contain 
a portion of the parishes in Thurgarton Wapentake. 

124, Chancery Lane^

Marriages at Radford, 

1563 to 1812. 

Note. ‚Äî The earlier volumes of Radford Registers are eleven in number, 
as follows : ‚Äî 

Vol. I. consists of 22} leaves of parchment^ measuring I2| by 

5 inches, stitched together in a parchment cover. The half-leaf, 
which has been divided longitudinally, occurs next after the 14th. 
The volume contains entries of Baptisms, 1563- 1653 ; Burials, 
1563- 1651 ; Marriages, 1563-1642. The chronology of all entries is 
badly confused. 

Vol. II. consists of 31 leaves of parchment, measuring I2| by 

6 inches, stitched together in a parchment cover. It contains entries 
of Baptisms, 1653-1702 ; Burials, 1653-1702 ; Marriages, 1654-1702. 

Vol. III. consists of 23 leaves of parchment (and a fragment of 
the 24th), measuring 12^ by 6i inches, stitched together in a parch- 
ment cover. It contains entries of Baptisms, 1703-1730; Burials, 
1703-1730; Marriages, 1703-1730. 

Vol. IV. consists of 28 leaves of parchment, measuring 13 by 
6| inches, bound in white leather covers. It contains entries of 
Baptisms, 1730-1776 ; Burials, 1730-1776 ; Marriages, 1730-1754. 

Vol, V. is a book of parchment forms, measuring 9I by 7J inches, 
two on each page (both sides being used), is bound in brown leather, 
and contains entries of Marriages and Banns only, commencing re- 
spectively at either end of the book. The former occupy 28 leaves, 
and cover the period 1754-1782. 

Vol. VI. is a book of paper forms, measuring 9| by 7^ inches, 
two on each page (one side only of paper used), is bound in white 
leather, and contains entries of Marriages and Banns only, com- 
mencing respectively at cither end of the book. The former occupy 
74 leaves, and cover the period 1782- 1799. The 73rd and 74th 
leaves are used on both sides. 

Vol. VII. is a thick l)ook of paper forms, measuring 16^ by 
10} inches, three on each page (one side only of paper used), is 
bound in brown leather, and contains entries of Marriages only, 
1799- 1 808. 

Vol. VIII. is similar in all respects to the last-named, except that 
it is slightly taller, and only the first half of the book has been used. 
It contains entries of Marriages only, 1808-1812. 

Notts ‚Äî IX. b 



2 Nottinghamshire Parish Registers. [1563 

Vol. IX. consists of 30 leaves of parchment, measuring 14 by 
8^ inches, bound in brown leather. It contains entries of Baptisms, 
1777-1799 ; Burials, I777-I794. 

Vol. X. consists of 32 leaves of parchment, measuring 13 by 
8} inches, bound in brown leather. It contains entries of Baptisms, 
1800-1807 ; Burials, 1794-1807. 

Vol. XI. consists of many parchment leaves, measuring 17 by 
io| inches, and bound in brown leather. The first five leaves 
contain entries of Baptisms, 1807-1812. Three leaves at opposite 
end of book contain entries of Burials, 1808-1812. 

These Marriages have been transcribed by Mr. A. Stapleton, of 
Nottingham, and are now printed under his supervision, by per- 
mission of the Rev. C. Lea Wilson, Vicar of Old Radford.

E 



Marriages at Hucknall 
Torkard, 

1559 to 1812. 

Note. ‚Äî The first volume of Hucknall Torkard registers consists of 56 
leaves of parchment, which has suffered much for want of a cover, 
the first two leaves being fragmentary, and the entries on the first 
and last pages of the book having been rubbed until almost illegible. 
The volume contains entries of Baptisms, Marriages and Burials 
from 1559 to 1686. The first part is a transcript of an earlier paper 
book very neatly and legibly copied by more than one hand. At 
several periods, such as 1592- 1625, about 1630, and 1642- 1652, the 
register has been very negligently kept, and entries are very sparse. 

The second volume consists of 13 parchment leaves, in a parch- 
ment cover, all loose, and contains Baptisms, Marriages, and Burials 
from 1696 to 1725. There are no entries between 1686 and 1696. 

The third volume is a small folio of 32 parchment leaves, bound 
in parchment boards, and containing Marriages from 1729 to I753> 
and Baptisms and Burials from 1726 to 1783 and 1782 respectively. 
At the end are copies of two Terriers of 1764 and 1777. 

The later volumes of the register are of the usual type. 

These marriages were copied by the late vicar of the parish, the 
Rev. J. E. Phillips, in 1897, and the proofs have been carefully 
collated with the originals, as regards the period 1559 to 1753 by 
Mr. T. M. Blagg, F.S.A., and from 1754 to 1812 by Mr. J. H. 
Beardsmore, of Hucknall Torkard. 

Volume I.

Marriages at Annesley, 

1599 to 1812. 

Note.‚Äî The oldest Register is a long narrow volume, vellum throughout, 
151 ins. long by 5| ins. wide, containing 32 pages. It is divided 
into three parts, which are occupied respectively by the Christenings, 
Marriages and Burials from the year 1599 to 1706. The bottom 
quarter of the outside co\ er is much destroyed by damp or insects, 
and the decay affects the inside corner all through the volume, but it 
is very nearly all quite legible with study. After the year 1699 all 
the entries are very much mixed up, and seem to have t>een put in 
wherever there was a blank place in the Register, and one or two are 
to be found re-entered in the next Register. The inscription on the 
front outside cover runs as follows :^ 

"Annesley Register made in the year of our Lord A.D. 
1600 by Thomas Kirkbie, then Curate here. John Breedon 
and Anthonie Pyamore, Churchwardens. 
Anesley." 
On the inside of the back cover occurs the following note : ‚Äî 

Mem.‚Äî Patricius, Lord Cbaworth married Lady Grace 
Manners, daug'' to the then Earl of Rutland. 
On the outside of the back cover there is some barely legible writing 
at the top, in which the words " Mansfield " and " Annesley " are plain. 
Below this come two notes as follows : ‚Äî 

"The marriage of Thomas Gilbert with Mary Stacey 
about the year 1694.** 

" Also the marriage of John (Breedon ?) with Ann Gilbert 
about the year 1705." 
Vol. II. is a t)ook 13 ins. by 7) ins., with vellum cover and 
leaves. It purports to have been bought in 171 1 ; if so, its earlier 
entries must have been copied in from other sources. Its first two 
pages are devoted to the registers of the baptisms of the " Chawot th " 
family from 1700-1726. The entries for the rest of the parish begin 
with 1706, with the exception of one wedding in 1701, which is 
re-entered from the oldest Register. The Baptisms and Burials go 
down to 1791, the Marriages to 1764. The last 30 Marriage entries 
occur over again in the next Register, fully signed by the parties 
married and two witnesses. 

The inscription on the fly-leaf is . ‚Äî 

"This book was bought Anno Domini 1711." 
Andrew Matthews, Curate. 



Joseph Barret, \^^ ^ 
William Bccston,/C^¬ª^^*'^*'^^¬´¬∞¬´ 



74 Nottinghamshire Parish Registers. [1599 

The inscription before the entries runs as follows : ‚Äî 

" Annesley Register, containing a true account of y Chris- 
tenings, Burials and Marriages in y said Pairish in y* days, 
months and years as followeth." 
Vol. III., contains Marriages, dates from 1754 to 1806. It 
is a paper book, rather the worse for wear, and without a cover. 
It is the same size as an ordinary Baptism Register now, and 
contains only Marriages and Banns. 

Vol. IV. takes the Marriages down to 1812. It is a square 
leather-bound volume, like a modem Banns book, and with the 
words common to all the entries printed. 

The Registers have been transcribed by the Rev. W H. 
Kynaston, the Vicar, and are now published with his permission. 
They have been collated by Mr. G. G. Bonser.

Marriages at Bulwell, 

1635 to 1812. 

Note. ‚Äî The Parish Registers of Bulwell containing Marriages are Ave 
in number. 

The first is a parchment volume of 25 pages, 15 ins. high and 
6 ins. wide¬ª bound in parchment ; the first page and the 23rd are 
partially cut away. It contains Baptisms, Marriages and BuriaU. 
The ceremonials are not kept separate ; the first entry is a Baptism 
on 6th April, 162 1, and the last a Baptism on 2nd May, 1703. 
Marriages and Burials begin 1635. 

The second register commences with this heading : ** A Register 
of Bull well, in the County of Nottingham, begun by me, Adam 
Turner, Rr. of Bullwell, from the time that I came to inhabit there," 
and was *' bought by Luke Haraman and Thomas Yarley, Church- 
wardens.*' It consists of 24 parchment leaves and one of paper, 
12 ins. high and 7I ins. wide, and contains mixed ceremonials from 
1702 to 1733. After the year 1717 the Baptisms, Marriages and 
Burials are kept separate. 

The third register is also a parchment volume of 20 pages, 17J Ins. 
high and 7| ins. wide, and contains mixed ceremonials from 1733 to 
1754, and the Baptisms and Burials continue on to 1776. 

The forth register is the usual paper volume of printed forms, and 
extends from 1754 to 1788. 

The fifth register is also a paper volume of printed forms, 7| ins. 
high and 9| ins. wide, and extends from 1789 to 181 2. The entries 
are continued on the back of the forms intended for k>anns, which are 
not filled up. 

These Marriages have t)een transcril>ed by Mr. F. A. Wadsworth, 
of Nottingham, and are now printed under his supervision by per- 
mission of the Rev. A. E. Rose, M.A., rector of the parish.

[Note at end of Vol. III. : Remarks on the 
** According to an Act of Parliament passed in 24th year of His 
Majesty's reign, and in the year of our Lord 1751, the old 
style ceases here and the new style takes place, and con- 
sequently the next which in the old account would have been 
the 3rd is now to be called the 14th, so that all the inter- 
mediate nominal days from the 2nd to the 14th are omitted or 
rather annihilated this year, and the month continues no more 
than 19 days, and year took place [for 1752] on the ist day 
of January."

I 2 



Marriages at Bunny 

1556 to 1818. 

Note. ‚Äî It was found impossible to transcribe these registers in time for 
their inclusion in their proper place ‚Äî the completing volume of 
Rushcliffe Wapentake. 

The Registers at Bunny begin in 1556 for all classes of entries. 
The Chapelry of Bradmore is attached to this living and the entries 
relating to its inhabitants are included in the registers of Bunny. 
Key worth and Thorpe-in-Glebis were also at some periods annexed 
to this parish. In this transcript ** Br." indicates Bradmore, " Ord. 
lie.'* means by licence from the Ordinary, in contradistinction to 
the Archbishop's or Vicar's licence. From 1556 to 1594 the year 
in these registers appears to have been computed as beginning from 
I January, though from 1594 to 1752 the usual method of dating 
from 25 March is adopted. 

These Marriages from 1638 to 1818 were copied by the Rev. H. 
Cooper, the late Vicar ; the earlier ones, from 1556 to 1637, have been 
done by Mr. T. M. Blagg, under whose supervision the whole are now 
printed by permission of the present Vicar, the Rev. S. G. O. Anderson.

Marriages at Langar, 



1596 to 1812. 

Note ‚Äî Langar Registers previous to 1813 consist of four volumes, all 
neatly bound in rough calf. 

Vol. I. consists of 51 leaves of parchment, measuring 13J by 5I 
inches and contains entries of Baptisms from 1595 to 1692, Marriages 
1596 to 1692 and Burials 1596 to 1678. Burials after 1678 are not 
entered in this volume, bee ause of the Act requiring affidavits to be 
made that the body was not " put in, wrapt or wound up, or buried, 
in any shirt, shift, sheet or shroud made ¬´ r mingled with flax, hemp, 
silk, hair, gold, or silver, or than what is made of sheep*s wool only ** 
As these affidavits, for the first portion of the period for which they 
were compulsory, are entered in Langar Registers at some length, 
with the name of the person making the affidavit, a separate volume 
was kept for Burial entries only, from 1678 to 1734. 

Vol. II. consists of 17 leaves of parchment 19 by 6f inches, con- 
taining Baptisms 1692 to 1763, Marriages 1694 to 1764 and Burials 
1735 to 1764, marginal memoranda of affidavits of burial in woollen 
aie entered from 173 S to 1753, when they cease. 

Vol. III. also of parchment, contains Baptisms, Marriages, and 
Burials from 1764 to 1812. It contains also some interesting notes 
and memoranda relatmg to the parish. 

Vol. IV. as above mentioned contains the Burials and affidavits 
from 1678 to 1734. It is of paper. 

These Marriages have been transcribed by Mr. T. M. Blagg, F.S.A. 
and are now printed under his supervision by permission of the 
Rector, the Kev. D. Fitz Herbert Wright.

[During the Commonwealth there are hardly any entries of 
marriages in Langar Registers, as that ceremony was per- 
formed before the Magistrates at Bingham. For instance, 
the marriage of William Flower in 1658 is also recorded in 
Bingham Registers as having taken place in the market there 
on August 6th. The woman's name is entered in the Bing- 
ham Registers as " Blauge." (See Vol. I, p. 3.)]
